< Review>
I rarely eat pizza; but my husband is one of those every-other-day types. He loves this pizza. Ordering online is simple, especially since he always likes the same 2 kinds. Order tracking is almost fun to keep up with (I'm old; I don't get out much!) and accurate on delivery time. We usually have the same young man deliver - consistency is nice! - and he is polite in a way rarely seen any more these days. All around a great experience. And on the rare occasions I do order for myself, a wonderful "Hawaiian" style is easy to build AND delicious! Highly recommend the Sierra College Blvd store, on the edge between Roseville and Granite Bay.< /Review>

<Date>1521987076817</Date>< Rating>
4<//Rating>
< Review>
Rosa Linda's is a very good local restaurant. They have another location in Fresno, but I've not eaten there yet. The dining room is modest in size. The food quality is exceptional. Their take on the traditional Mexican food is very good with sauces that have their own touch of flavor that sets them apart from other Mexican restaurants in the area. My wife loves the soups. I like their "Selma Tacos" (and every other menu item!) The one drawback to the atmosphere in the restaurant is that when they are busy it is quite noisy with conversations reverberating across the room and it can be difficult to hear conversation at your own table.</Review>

I typically drive to redlands to get my indian food fix, but decided to try Namaste one evening and was pleasantly surprised.
There is a great mix of ready-made options available as well as a great offering of menu items that can be made on request.  There is also a nice variety of vegetarian dishes.  I particularly loved the daal, aloo gobi, and chana masala.
Garlic Naan was amazing, portion sizes are generous, and the prices will keep you going back.
I typically eat indian food once every month or two, and came back here twice in a week, it was that good!
They are also very kid friendly, so much that our three year old has asked to go back.  I highly recommend them!</review>

<Text>My car suddenly started making loud noises, and then my check engine light came on, so I was concerned that it was something serious. Since it was right after Christmas I was also concerned about how much it would cost. I looked around online for someone locally and started reading the different reviews. They mentioned that this place was honest and did great work. When I got there, there were a few people ahead of me, and more kept showing up, it was also close to lunch time, so I was concerned that it would take long for my car to get checked and worked on. A few minutes later my car was lifted and looked at, and the manager Paul told me, that my issue was not serious, it was only the oxygen sensor that had come loose, and it would only cost $30 for them to have it fixed. It's true, the manager Paul is very honest! They could have made up a story and told me it was something more serious to charge me more, but he didn't. My car was quickly fixed, and sounds normal now. I can see why people take the time to write good reviews about this place. < Review>
Gluten free poke! That's astoundingly hard to find in this area, since a lot of poke fish comes pre-dressed in sauce. The "build your own" option here is incredible because every ingredient is specifically listed for allergens! There are also tons of topping options and sauces. In light of the pandemic, we've gotten takeout and delivery from Poke Poke pretty frequently, and it's always well packaged and fresh. The value is great for the quantity of fish you get - I've never gotten the chipotle feeling of "damn, those portion spoons were small today ". Love Poke Poke and can't wait to come back soon!< /Review>

< Review>
If you love sushi, you are going to love poke.  It's like a Chipotle, but for sushi.  You start with a Bowl of sushi rice (brown rice and veggie option also available) and then add the various types of sushi, sauces and toppings like seaweed. The fish is fresh and overall quality is really good.  I've been a dozen times in the last two months.  What's most surprising is this is the only one in the greater KC area that I know of.  These poke bars are all over California, Chicago, Dallas and other major metros.<//Review>

<user_id>114183164321661693007</user_id><date>1609645475567< /date><Rating>5< /Rating><response>None< /response><Pictures>None<//Pictures><name>VI V. VO<//name>< text>
I have two favorite poke places: Pokehouse and Go Fish. PokePoke is definitely a very close runner up.

SERVICE
It was my first time here and after I started asking what the fish were the person who helped me noticed that I was unfamiliar and was very through with me until the end when I got my toppings. I want to say the service here is excellent, compared to Pokehouse where they get so many orders that they just don't care and wait for you to figure it out yourself. At PokePoke, my server started listing all that they had toppings wise because there weren't signage nor were they easily identifiable. I think that small notion of trying to be helpful got to me. I usually don't tip the first time I go places and usually tip my 2nd time around but this was one of the few places I tipped on the first visit and a bit extra too.

FOOD QUALITY
I am in LOVE with the yam noodles here. It is incomparable to GoFish. PokePoke has the best yam noodles hands down. Pokehouse doesn't even have that option.
My fish weren't warm and the toppings were plentiful in variety; HOWEVER I wish it were the same with the protein. I love octopus and tofu options and sadly they didn't have it. I did notice that they had both regular and spicy crab salad, and yellowtail which is very nice. Unagi would've been a great addition too but that's more difficult as opposed to the traditional ahi and salmon. I adored their little sauce list too, although I wish they added sauce to the yam noodles as they were quite bland for me. Honestly, if their were more variety with protein, (for toppings they had cheetos and carrot/daikon which are unique and I love it) this would be my #1 go to.

Everytime my portion fell out the small scoop my server would always go back and scoop up what fell with a bit more. And it's such a small gesture but the fact it happened at all makes me grateful. I DEFINITELY will come back sometime soon.</text>

< Review>
Food was good but not worth the price (cheaper poke elsewhere in the area that's just as great). Pricing on their menu was completely off so I was surprised with the total when I got my bill. They had a special that clearly stated that you could order a 4 piece California or spicy tuna roll for $2 so I asked to add one to my order. When the cashier rang up my total, it was $28! For one bowl and a 4 piece California roll. When I asked the cashier about it, she was completely confused and then said "oh you can get two of the 4 pieces for that price". <user>106051614928980993994</user>< review>
Although there may be many poke places now around the bay area, this place serves a great variety of fishes and has many different options for toppings!

For a poke bowl, price can range from $11-15 for a regular bowl (depending if you want additional items). They also have house specials and allow you to sample the fishes or flavors if you would like. If you get a poke bowl, you can choose between brown rice, mixed greens, or half brown rice and half mixed green, 3 fishes/shrimp, and unlimited toppings.
I would suggest to sample he house special for one of the options of fishes. I loved it! They also have variety of sauces and add more toppings after you finish your bowl. Toppings may include furikake, tofu crunches, garlic crunches and more (sorry, I'm not sure what those "crouton-like" toppings are called)! Great seating area with lots of tables compared to other poke bowl places and amazing customer service! My friends and I came around 1 P.M. on a weekday and you can definitely tell the place gets packed during lunch hours and dinner time.< /review>

<name>Carolyn Allen</name>< Time>
1488972986342</Time>
< rate>
4< /rate>
< review>
I've been to a lot of poke places, but this one has got their act together! The service is really fast because the staff asks questions such as "would you like any cucumber, green peppers and furikake?  Would you like salmon and tuna?  Avocado and seaweed salad?"  Etc. Etc.  The questions are helpful and efficient because customers don't have to stare at the toppings and try to figure out what the toppings are.

As for the food itself, it has gotta be one of the best poke places I've tried in the Bay Area.  Everything is EXTREMELY fresh and not mushy in any way.  The vegetables are sweet and crunchy, and the fish doesn't smell fishy at all.  The sauces go well together and they have a side bar where you are free to add as many extra crunchy toppings as you'd like.  The side bar contains extra spicy mayo sauce, furikake, and other sauces that you can add yourself if you feel like their servers didn't add enough - Also great because you don't need to go back to the servers to ask them to add more!

I think this is by far the most efficiently set up poke joint I've visited.  The delicious, fresh food is one of the reasons why I'll be sure to visit this place again!< /review>

<Review>This was my go-to poke place for the last 3 months... that is, until last night. The last two visits were atrocious, thus I'm downgrading my rating. Poke Poke Fish Bar started out strong. Portion size was large; their sauces are really good. Toppings weren't anything to write home about, but you can't win everything. But recently, they have been very inconsistent. Maybe it's because they've been training a few new people. But the portion I got last night was at least 25% less than usual. That's not okay. There were like maybe 5-6 pieces of fish per scoop. <Name>Gary Chow<//Name><Gmap_id>0x808fca4054e7532f:0x26ccd720bf39daa4</Gmap_id><UserId.>104539715813332020581< /UserId.><review>One of the newer poke bowl restaurants in the area, Poke Poke is staffed by friendly, patient people who are happy to answer all the inevitable questions that people may have about their bowl.

Start with your base; there's rice, yam noodles, salad (maybe more, but I don't venture beyond this).  You can get dressing on your salad, and you have a choice between regular and spicy krab (yes, with a "K") meat.  Pick your poke and sauce; scoops are reasonably large, though maybe it's because the fish cubes look bigger than from some other places.  There are a multitude of toppings you can add, including  cucumber, onions, mango and kimchi, just to name a few.  Finish it off with crunchy toppings, such as fried won ton skins, tempura flakes/ and furikake.  What seems to set this place apart is that they really try to fill your bowl to the top, which is a refreshing change from the sometimes half full bowls that other places sometimes serve.  And there are actually a fair number of tables you can sit and enjoy your poke.

To top it all off, since this used to be a pinkberry, you can also get FroYo here.

The quality of the ingredients (i.e., fish) is pretty good; not necessarily the best around, but a strong contender.  Definitely worth a try if you are in the area and want some poke.<//review><pics>None< /pics></record>

<Time>1489646734509< /Time><rate>4<//rate><text>One of the newer poke bowl restaurants in the area, Poke Poke is staffed by friendly, patient people who are happy to answer all the inevitable questions that people may have about their bowl.

Start with your base; there's rice, yam noodles, salad (maybe more, but I don't venture beyond this).  You can get dressing on your salad, and you have a choice between regular and spicy krab (yes, with a "K") meat.  Pick your poke and sauce; scoops are reasonably large, though maybe it's because the fish cubes look bigger than from some other places.  There are a multitude of toppings you can add, including  cucumber, onions, mango and kimchi, just to name a few.  Finish it off with crunchy toppings, such as fried won ton skins, tempura flakes/ and furikake.  What seems to set this place apart is that they really try to fill your bowl to the top, which is a refreshing change from the sometimes half full bowls that other places sometimes serve.  And there are actually a fair number of tables you can sit and enjoy your poke.

To top it all off, since this used to be a pinkberry, you can also get FroYo here.

The quality of the ingredients (i.e., fish) is pretty good; not necessarily the best around, but a strong contender.  Definitely worth a try if you are in the area and want some poke.<//text>< pictures>
